<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="hd" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: transparent">Father's Day</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans_-_Paternal_advice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Josephus Laurentius Dyckmans - Paternal advice.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans_-_Paternal_advice.jpg/240px-Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans_-_Paternal_advice.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="300" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans_-_Paternal_advice.jpg/360px-Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans_-_Paternal_advice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans_-_Paternal_advice.jpg/480px-Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans_-_Paternal_advice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="811" data-file-height="1015" /></a><div style="caption"><i>Paternal advice</i><br /><a href="/wiki/Josephus_Laurentius_Dyckmans" title="Josephus Laurentius Dyckmans">Josephus Laurentius Dyckmans</a></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Observed&#160;by</th><td>111+ countries</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Type</th><td>Worldwide</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Significance</th><td class="summary">Honors fathers and fatherhood</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date</th><td>Varies per country</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Frequency</th><td>Annual</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Related&#160;to</th><td><a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Day" title="Children&#39;s Day">Children's Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siblings_Day" title="Siblings Day">Siblings Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day" title="Mother&#39;s Day">Mother's Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parents%27_Day" title="Parents&#39; Day">Parents' Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Grandparents_Day" title="National Grandparents Day">Grandparents Day</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Father's Day</b> is a celebration honoring fathers and celebrating fatherhood, paternal bonds and the influence of fathers in society. In Catholic countries of Europe, it has been celebrated on March 19 (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph&#39;s Day">Saint Joseph's Day</a>) since the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. This celebration was brought by the Spanish and Portuguese to <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, where March 19 is often still used for it, though many countries in Europe and the Americas have adopted the U.S. date, which is the third Sunday of June. It is celebrated on various days in many parts of the world, most commonly in the months of March, April and June according to the home nation's customs. It complements similar celebrations honoring family members, such as <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day" title="Mother&#39;s Day">Mother's Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siblings_Day" title="Siblings Day">Siblings Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grandparents_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Grandparents Day">Grandparents' Day</a>.
</p><p>In its modern form it was founded by <a href="/wiki/Sonora_Smart_Dodd" title="Sonora Smart Dodd">Sonora Smart Dodd</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A customary day for the celebration of fatherhood in <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> is known to date back to at least 1508. It is observed on <a href="/wiki/March_19" title="March 19">March 19</a>, as the feast day of Saint Joseph, who is referred to as the fatherly <i>Nutritor Domini</i> ("Nourisher of the Lord") in Catholicism and "the putative father of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>" in southern European tradition. This celebration was brought to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> actively supported the custom of a celebration of fatherhood on St. Joseph's Day from either the last years of the <a href="/wiki/14th_century" title="14th century">14th century</a> or from the early <a href="/wiki/15th_century" title="15th century">15th century</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-natgeo_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> apparently on the initiative of the <a href="/wiki/Franciscans" title="Franciscans">Franciscans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">Coptic Church</a>, the celebration of fatherhood is also observed on St Joseph's Day, but the Copts observe this celebration on July 20. This Coptic celebration may date back to the fifth century.<sup id="cite_ref-natgeo_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_United_States">In the United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: In the United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings">Beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Father's Day was not celebrated in the US, outside Catholic traditions, until the 20th century. As a civic celebration in the US, it was inaugurated in the early 20th century to complement <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day" title="Mother&#39;s Day">Mother's Day</a> by celebrating fathers and male <a href="/wiki/Parenting" title="Parenting">parenting</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg/220px-USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg/330px-USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg/440px-USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5274" data-file-height="3516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC-120617-M-3042W-938.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During the Father's Day luncheon held at the Pacific Views Event Center, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Pendleton" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton">Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton</a></div></div></div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Anna_Jarvis" title="Anna Jarvis">Anna Jarvis</a>' successful promotion of Mother's Day in <a href="/wiki/Grafton,_West_Virginia" title="Grafton, West Virginia">Grafton, West Virginia</a>, the first observance of a day honoring fathers was held on July 5, 1908, in <a href="/wiki/Fairmont,_West_Virginia" title="Fairmont, West Virginia">Fairmont, West Virginia</a>, in the Williams Memorial Methodist Episcopal Church South, now known as Central <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="United Methodist">United Methodist</a> Church.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_185_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_185-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Grace Golden Clayton was mourning the loss of her father, when in December 1907, the <a href="/wiki/Monongah_Mining_Disaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Monongah Mining Disaster">Monongah Mining Disaster</a> in nearby <a href="/wiki/Monongah,_West_Virginia" title="Monongah, West Virginia">Monongah</a> killed 361 men, 250 of them fathers, leaving around a thousand fatherless children. Clayton suggested that her pastor Robert Thomas Webb honor all those fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-Butler2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Butler2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wvah2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wvah2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wvah1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wvah1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-first_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Clayton's event did not have repercussions outside Fairmont for several reasons; among them were the city was overwhelmed by other events, the celebration was never promoted outside the town itself, and no proclamation of it was made by the city council. Also, two events overshadowed this event: the celebration of <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">Independence Day</a> July 4, 1908, with 12,000 attendants and several shows, including a hot-air balloon event, which took over the headlines in the following days, and the death of a 16-year-old girl on July 4. The local church and council were overwhelmed and they did not even think of promoting the event, and it was not celebrated again for many years. The original sermon was not reproduced by the press and it was lost. Finally, Clayton was a quiet person, who never promoted the event and never talked to other persons about it.<sup id="cite_ref-wvah2_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wvah2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wvah1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wvah1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-first_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Failed_attempts_at_establishing_a_Father.27s_Day"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Failed_attempts_at_establishing_a_Father's_Day">Failed attempts at establishing a Father's Day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Failed attempts at establishing a Father&#039;s Day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1911, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Addams" title="Jane Addams">Jane Addams</a> proposed that a citywide Father's Day celebration be held in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, but she was turned down.<sup id="cite_ref-larossa_first_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-larossa_first-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1912,  a Father's Day celebration was held in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver,_Washington" title="Vancouver, Washington">Vancouver, Washington</a>, suggested by Methodist pastor J.J. Berringer of the Irvington Methodist Church. They mistakenly believed that they had been the first to celebrate such a day.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_185_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_185-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> They followed a 1911 suggestion by the <i><a href="/wiki/Portland_Oregonian" class="mw-redirect" title="Portland Oregonian">Portland Oregonian</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-larossa_first_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-larossa_first-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Harry C. Meek, a member of <a href="/wiki/Lions_Clubs_International" title="Lions Clubs International">Lions Clubs International</a>, claimed that he had first come up with the idea for Father's Day in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_185_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_185-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-larossa_first_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-larossa_first-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Meek said that the third Sunday in June was chosen because it was his birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-larossa_first_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-larossa_first-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Lions Club has named him the "Originator of Father's Day".<sup id="cite_ref-myers_185_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_185-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Meek made many efforts to promote Father's Day and make it an official holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_185_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_185-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-larossa_first_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-larossa_first-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_of_the_holiday">Establishment of the holiday</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Establishment of the holiday">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On June 19, 1910, a Father's Day celebration was held at the <a href="/wiki/YMCA" title="YMCA">YMCA</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spokane,_Washington" title="Spokane, Washington">Spokane, Washington</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Sonora_Smart_Dodd" title="Sonora Smart Dodd">Sonora Smart Dodd</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Schmidt_276_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmidt_276-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Father&#39;s_Day_United_States_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Father&#39;s_Day_United_States-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Her father, the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">civil war</a> veteran <a href="/wiki/William_Jackson_Smart" class="mw-redirect" title="William Jackson Smart">William Jackson Smart</a>, was a single parent who raised his six children there.<sup id="cite_ref-Schmidt_276_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmidt_276-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> She was also a member of Old Centenary Presbyterian Church (now Knox Presbyterian Church),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> where she first proposed the idea. After hearing a <a href="/wiki/Sermon" title="Sermon">sermon</a> about Jarvis' Mother's Day in 1909 at Central Methodist Episcopal Church, she told her <a href="/wiki/Elder_(Methodism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elder (Methodism)">pastor</a> that fathers should have a similar holiday to honor them.<sup id="cite_ref-Schmidt_276_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmidt_276-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Although she initially suggested June 5, her father's birthday, the pastors did not have enough time to prepare their sermons, and the celebration was deferred to the third Sunday in June.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_185_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_185-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-larossa_first_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-larossa_first-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Several local clergymen accepted the idea, and on June 19, 1910, the first Father's Day, "sermons honoring fathers were presented throughout the city".<sup id="cite_ref-Butler_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Butler-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Father_with_tow_baby.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Father_with_tow_baby.jpg/200px-Father_with_tow_baby.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Father_with_tow_baby.jpg/300px-Father_with_tow_baby.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Father_with_tow_baby.jpg/400px-Father_with_tow_baby.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Father_with_tow_baby.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladeshi</a> father with son and daughter</div></div></div>
<p>However, in the 1920s, Dodd stopped promoting the celebration because she was studying at the <a href="/wiki/Art_Institute_of_Chicago" title="Art Institute of Chicago">Art Institute of Chicago</a>, and it faded into relative obscurity, even in Spokane.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the 1930s, Dodd returned to Spokane and started promoting the celebration again, raising awareness at a national level.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> She had the help of those trade groups that would benefit most from the holiday, for example the manufacturers of ties, tobacco pipes, and any traditional presents for fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> By 1938, she had the help of the Father's Day Council, founded by the New York Associated Men's Wear Retailers to consolidate and systematize the holiday's commercial promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Americans resisted the holiday for its first few decades, viewing it as nothing more than an attempt by merchants to replicate the commercial success of Mother's Day, and newspapers frequently featured cynical and sarcastic attacks and jokes.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> However, the said merchants remained resilient and even incorporated these attacks into their advertisements.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> By the mid-1980s, the Father's Day Council wrote, "(...) [Father's Day] has become a Second Christmas for all the men's gift-oriented industries."<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vaderdag07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Vaderdag07.jpg/220px-Vaderdag07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Vaderdag07.jpg/330px-Vaderdag07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Vaderdag07.jpg/440px-Vaderdag07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vaderdag07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Father's Day in <a href="/wiki/Deventer" title="Deventer">Deventer</a>, Netherlands</div></div></div>
<p>A bill to accord national recognition of the holiday was introduced in Congress in 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt1913_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1913-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1916, President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> went to Spokane to speak at a Father's Day celebration<sup id="cite_ref-myers_186_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_186-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and he wanted to make it an officially recognized  federal holiday, but Congress resisted, fearing that it would become commercialized.<sup id="cite_ref-daily_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daily-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> US president <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Coolidge" title="Calvin Coolidge">Calvin Coolidge</a> recommended in 1924 that the day be observed throughout the entire nation, but he stopped short at issuing a national proclamation.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_186_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_186-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Two earlier attempts to formally recognize the holiday had been defeated by Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_186_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_186-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nashua_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nashua-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 1957, Maine senator <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Chase_Smith" title="Margaret Chase Smith">Margaret Chase Smith</a> wrote a Father's Day proposal accusing Congress of ignoring fathers for 40 years while honoring mothers, thus "[singling] out just one of our two parents".<sup id="cite_ref-nashua_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nashua-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 1966, President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> issued the first presidential proclamation honoring fathers, designating the third Sunday in June as Father's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-daily_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daily-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Six years later, the day was made a permanent national holiday when President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> signed it into law in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-myers_186_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myers_186-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-daily_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daily-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nashua_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nashua-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to Father's Day, <a href="/wiki/International_Men%27s_Day" title="International Men&#39;s Day">International Men's Day</a> is celebrated in many countries on November 19 in honor of men and boys.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spelling">Spelling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Spelling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the United States, Dodd used the "Fathers' Day" spelling on her original petition for the holiday,<sup id="cite_ref-Schmidt_276_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmidt_276-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> but the spelling "Father's Day" was already used in 1913 when a bill was introduced to the U.S. Congress as the first attempt to establish the holiday,<sup id="cite_ref-nyt1913_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1913-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and it was still spelled the same way when its creator was commended in 2008 by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dates_around_the_world">Dates around the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Father%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dates around the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The officially recognized date of Father's Day varies from country to country. This section lists some significant examples, in order of date of observance.

//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Flag_of_Qatar.svg/46px-Flag_of_Qatar.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="550" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> <br /><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/23px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> <br /><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flag_of_Yemen.svg/23px-Flag_of_Yemen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> <br /><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Flag_of_Syria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Syria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" title="Syria">Syria</a> <br /><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_Somalia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Somalia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23"
